        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1454019383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16383291791668601194">Continuing from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454019337' rel='nofollow noopener'>my review of <i>Twilight</i></a>, I'm going to refute points that claim that <i>Twilight</i> is better than <i>Harry Potter</i>. <br/><br/>I repeat, I'm only posting this because I read <a href='http://ohnotheydidnt.livejournal.com/61244302.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>this article</a>. I'm literally only refuting the points mentioned in this, nothing else. I don't like comparison, but if the other party does it, be sure that I will respond. <br/><br/><b>
  <u>REBUTTAL POINTS 11-20:</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>11. In harry potter all they do is fly around on brooms and kill people with magic sticks (wands) I mean, really?</b><br/>In <i>Twilight</i>, all they </span>
  <span id="freeText16383291791668601194" style="display:none">Continuing from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454019337" rel="nofollow noopener">my review of <i>Twilight</i></a>, I'm going to refute points that claim that <i>Twilight</i> is better than <i>Harry Potter</i>. <br /><br />I repeat, I'm only posting this because I read <a href="http://ohnotheydidnt.livejournal.com/61244302.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this article</a>. I'm literally only refuting the points mentioned in this, nothing else. I don't like comparison, but if the other party does it, be sure that I will respond. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>REBUTTAL POINTS 11-20:</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>11. In harry potter all they do is fly around on brooms and kill people with magic sticks (wands) I mean, really?</b><br />In <i>Twilight</i>, all they do is lust after each other and play baseball. I mean, really? <br /><br />In defence of <i>Harry Potter</i>, though, they also learn magic, give exams, celebrate Christmas and Halloween, deal with loss, deal with horrible teachers, plan their careers, protect the downtrodden (remember SPEW), participate in duels, watch Quidditch, play Quidditch, go to Hogsmeade, learn to make potions, and more importantly, learn of the importance of human relationships. I could go on, but I'm sure you get the gist.<br /><br /><b>12. Edward wasn't a dork. Yeah, sometimes, dorks are cute. However, Harry was a bit too dorky and I can't see why girls even liked him.</b><br />No, Edward wasn't a dork. He was just an asshole paedophile who wanted to fuck a virgin. And yes, dorks are adorable (going by what I assume dorks are, anyway). My (most recent) ex is a dork...? and he is genuinely one of the best people I know. Harry was also, as you put it, dorky, but he was a good person. You see, normal girls like good people. <br /><br />By this point, I'm honestly wondering what the relevance of all this is in proving that <i>Twilight</i> is superior, because honestly, none of these points are even remotely sensible. But my momma didn't raise a quitter, so I trudge along.<br /><br /><b>13. Harry Potter is for virgin nerds. Twilight is for cool and mature people.</b><br />How refreshingly mature of you! Not. *rolls eyes* Honestly, I'm definitely more mature than you are if this is the best you can come up with. <br /><br /><b>14. Hermione is a week character. Unline Bella, who struggles every day. Hermione has no problems, the only things she has are self-created. She follows Harry into his troubles. Big whoop. Even if she is teased about being a mud blood or whatever its called, she has a choice. She could quit Hogwarts or something. Bella has no choice, she is in love.</b><br />I'm sorry, what? You take that back right now!!! Are you actually serious about this? Hermione Granger is an inspiration to girls everywhere. She is smart, confident, independent, kind, compassionate, and one of the most amazing fictional characters to ever bless us. She doesn't have problems that 'she's created', she knows the sacrifices that she has to make for the greater good of the people. Bella doesn't even make sacrifices for her family (except Edward, but that's mostly because she wants the big D)! She doesn't follow Harry anywhere. She chooses to help him bring order into the world. She chooses to fight evil because that's who she is, a good person. And the whole mud-blood issue that you so carelessly trivialise has a much deeper connotaion in dealing with the stigma that people face for being different. She wouldn't quit Hogwarts, she's not a quitter. Besides, we don't see her complaining, do we? To paraphrase Hagrid, NEVER. INSULT. HERMIONE. GRANGER. IN. FRONT. OF. ME. And what bullshit! Bella of course, has a choice. She's just a co-dependent mope who cannot live on her own. <s>Love</s> Lust vs. the greater good. Hmm...tough choice there. <br /><br /><b>15. Twilight was a best selling novel, and has a bigger fan base than Harry Potter.</b><br />You know as well as I do that <i>Harry Potter</i> has sold more copies. This actually goes against your own argument. Oh, and <i>Harry Potter</i> definitely has a better and much larger fan base. In my own house, everyone from my grandmother to my second cousin once removed has read and enjoyed <i>Harry Potter</i>, while I'm the only one who's subjected myself to <s>medieval torture</s> the <i>Twilight</i> series. There's also <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/newsbeat/article/38101262/syrian-girl-thanks-jk-rowling-for-sending-harry-potter-books " rel="nofollow noopener">this gesture</a>.<br /><br /><b>16. Stephenie Meyer writes that the only thing that can kill a vampire is another vampire or a werewolf. Since Edward is a vampire created by Meyer, we can use her written characteristics and apply them to Harry Potter. Since Harry Potter is neither vampire nor wolf, this means that Harry Potter could not kill Edward and Edward would win.</b><br />Finally, a point that makes remote sense. Okay, first of all, why would you assume that there are no werewolves in <i>Harry Potter</i>? There's Remus Lupin, who is my all time favourite <i>Harry Potter</i> character. There are also actual evil werewolves like Fenrir Greyback who would be more than happy to kill your precious Edward. There are other vampires in Harry Potter also, but we never really pay much attention to them. I wonder why?! Alternately, because you're bringing Edward into a world created by Rowling, where all magical creatures more or less have those powers that are traditionally credited to them, a vampire may be destroyed by using methods that one would usually use to purge such undead. Think garlic, holy water, or the holy cross. Either way, you lose. <br /><br /><b>17. Twilight led to many other supernatural romances in books and tv shows.</b><br />Actually, if my knowledge is to be trusted (and it is), every other vampire-related show/book/work I've come across predates <i>Twilight</i>. <br /><br /><b>18. Unlike Harry, nobody's thoughts are actually that deep or intellectual. I bet if any of us published our thoughts into a book, none would be great English lit; Bella's thoughts are more realistic.</b><br />Harry's thoughts aren't really deep and intellectual either. Granted, he's a lot smarter than Bella; the troll in <i>Philosopher's Stone</i> is smarter than Bella, honestly, but he thinks just like anyone else would. Bella's thoughts are either along the lines of "I HAZ LUSSSSST" or "everything sucks". Hate to break it to ya, darling, but Bella's thoughts are insipid, and that's me putting it kindly. <br /><br /><b>19. at least all of them dosent a scar of a lightning bolt.</b><br />At least all of them aren't sparkly vampires. (Also, did we read the same <i>Harry Potter</i>, because if my memory serves me right, only one of them, i.e., Harry has a lightning bolt scar.)<br /><br /><b>20. no witchcraft (practicing witchcraft is bad).</b><br />I have come to the point of praying that these reasons have some element of sarcasm to them. Okay, let me break this down for you. It's pure fiction. Besides, if you think witchcraft is bad, shouldn't you think vampirism is bad? Seeing as how it is actually a sub culture where people bite each other and drink each other's blood? It might do you good to look into Richard Chase, aka the "Vampire of Sacramento", one of America's most prolific serial killers. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454019337" rel="nofollow noopener">Click here for my review of <i>Twilight</i> which contains points 1-10.</a><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454019415" rel="nofollow noopener">Click here for my review of <i>Eclipse</i>, which contains points 21-30.</a><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454019452" rel="nofollow noopener">Click here for my review of <i>Breaking Dawn</i>, which contains points 31-40.</a><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1822076006" rel="nofollow noopener">Click here for my review of the series, which contains points 41-46.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16383291791668601194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jvDg4fvIvDcXNYzRdWqOJX+tlxEtpJCnTF3TFUJEwsQGh0yU/DJjFmc6K8tlK6SZeG27frmLsrtf/KNRd45VUg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wTo3diHT5ta0wtba9fwAzFDxiqZZD6+F/uOKmAupyVFJTZsDJik598TNccDlvSpwVzGmyc0gjZntQvrcPmNexw==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText1357916935819711025" style="display:none">Stephenie Meyer is the author of the bestselling <i>Twilight</i> series, <i>The Host</i>, and <i>The Chemist</i>. <i>Twilight</i> was one of 2005's most talked about novels and within weeks of its release the book debuted at #5 on The New York Times bestseller list. Among its many accolades, <i>Twilight</i> was named an "ALA Top Ten Books for Young Adults," an Amazon.com "Best Book of the Decade So Far," and a Publishers Weekly Best Book of the Year. <br /><br />Meyer graduated from Brigham Young University with a degree in English Literature. She lives in Arizona with her husband and three sons.</span>
